          <div class="section-inner sectionLayout--insetColumn">
           <h1 name="20cf" id="20cf" class="graf graf--h3 graf--leading graf--title">How to Build the Trump Twitter Sentiment Analysis Dashboard</h1>
           <h2 name="ed25" id="ed25" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--h3 graf--subtitle">Analyze &amp; visualize how the Twittersphere feels about Trump in real-time.</h2>
           <figure name="6bdb" id="6bdb" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--h4">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 614px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 87.7%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*d_i_gD52jeJi71ihWIt9rA.gif" data-width="860" data-height="754" data-action="zoom" data-action-value="1*d_i_gD52jeJi71ihWIt9rA.gif">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*d_i_gD52jeJi71ihWIt9rA.gif?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*d_i_gD52jeJi71ihWIt9rA.gif">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*d_i_gD52jeJi71ihWIt9rA.gif">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="b329" id="b329" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">A world of hot takes, Twitter is just one of the many virtual environments that we can analyze 6,000 tweets per second to better understand how the world feels about a certain topic. It’s 2017, so naturally we’re going to gauge <a href="https://extranewsfeed.com/presidential-things/home" data-href="https://extranewsfeed.com/presidential-things/home" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">the world’s sentiment of Donald Trump</a>. Then we’ll visualize it.</p>
           <p name="bd48" id="bd48" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">The folks at <a href="https://www.initialstate.com/" data-href="https://www.initialstate.com/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Initial State</a>, a platform for building data visualizations, made this a reality, and it’s awesome. Combining Twitter’s API, PubNub, IBM Watson and Initial State, they were able to build a live Twitter dashboard that streams the tweets in realtime, analyzes and gauges the sentiment of the tweets, and publishes them in a number of different ways to the visualization.</p>
           <p name="2684" id="2684" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">And even better, there’s a full tutorial on how to build it. With that, read on!</p>
           <h3 name="d442" id="d442" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">Tutorial Overview</h3>
           <p name="73bc" id="73bc" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3"><em class="markup--em markup--p-em">This tutorial was written by </em><a href="https://www.linkedin.com/in/rcgibbs/" data-href="https://www.linkedin.com/in/rcgibbs/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><em class="markup--em markup--p-em">Rachel Gregory</em></a><em class="markup--em markup--p-em">, Customer Developer Lead at Initial State. She writes a ton of kickass tutorials, </em><a href="http://blog.initialstate.com/category/tutorials-3/" data-href="http://blog.initialstate.com/category/tutorials-3/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><em class="markup--em markup--p-em">check them out</em></a><em class="markup--em markup--p-em">.</em></p>
           <p name="aade" id="aade" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">This project makes heavy use of PubNub BLOCKS, which provides a serverless environment for executing functions on your data in motion (in this case, executing functions on each tweet that comes from the Twitter API via PubNub).</p>
           <h4 name="e42f" id="e42f" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Technology</h4>
           <ul class="postList">
            <li name="14f0" id="14f0" class="graf graf--li graf-after--h4"><strong class="markup--strong markup--li-strong">Twitter API</strong>: source of the tweets</li>
            <li name="ebfa" id="ebfa" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li"><strong class="markup--strong markup--li-strong">IBM Watson Sentiment Analysis BLOCK</strong>: this API allows you to analyze and gauge emotion, and determine where a text input sits on a negative-positive scale</li>
            <li name="4213" id="4213" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li"><strong class="markup--strong markup--li-strong">PubNub</strong>: streams the data from Twitter, processes the tweet with IBM Watson, and publishes the data to the Initial State dashboard</li>
            <li name="0bc4" id="0bc4" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li"><strong class="markup--strong markup--li-strong">Initial State</strong>: visualizes the data in a beautiful, live-updating dashboard</li>
           </ul>
           <h4 name="94c8" id="94c8" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--li">What we’ll&nbsp;cover</h4>
           <ul class="postList">
            <li name="be13" id="be13" class="graf graf--li graf-after--h4">Consuming the Twitter API to filter tweets by keyword with PubNub</li>
            <li name="0e4b" id="0e4b" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li">Gauging sentiment with the PubNub Sentiment Analysis BLOCK powered by IBM Watson.</li>
            <li name="ce84" id="ce84" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li">Sending results through BLOCKS to Initial State’s realtime dashboards</li>
            <li name="405c" id="405c" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li">Building the informative and interactive dashboard</li>
           </ul>
           <p name="8792" id="8792" class="graf graf--p graf-after--li graf--trailing">If you want to check out the <a href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard" data-href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">source code in its entirety, it’s available here</a>. Now, onto the tutorial!</p>
          </div>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section name="5745" class="section section--body">
         <div class="section-divider">
          <hr class="section-divider">

           <h3 name="dffa" id="dffa" class="graf graf--h3 graf--leading">Part 1?—?PubNub&nbsp;Setup</h3>
           <figure name="ffe2" id="ffe2" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--h3">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 449px; max-height: 101px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 22.5%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*xRqnal51nTrRVacfYbUKJQ.png" data-width="449" data-height="101">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*xRqnal51nTrRVacfYbUKJQ.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*xRqnal51nTrRVacfYbUKJQ.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*xRqnal51nTrRVacfYbUKJQ.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="c1bd" id="c1bd" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">The key to this entire project is <a href="https://www.pubnub.com/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" data-href="https://www.pubnub.com/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">PubNub</a>. Their slogan, “Realtime Apps Made Simple”, is true. They provide over 70 <a href="https://www.pubnub.com/docs#all-sdks-home?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" data-href="https://www.pubnub.com/docs#all-sdks-home?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">SDKs</a> and have plenty of pre-connected services in the form of <a href="https://www.pubnub.com/products/blocks/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" data-href="https://www.pubnub.com/products/blocks/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">BLOCKS</a>. These blocks are basically bits of code that process your data before or after it’s sent to it’s destination?—?no server needed!</p>
           <p name="67a0" id="67a0" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">We will be using both the <a href="https://www.pubnub.com/blocks-catalog/group-sentiment-analysis/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" data-href="https://www.pubnub.com/blocks-catalog/group-sentiment-analysis/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">IBM Watson Sentiment Analysis BLOCK</a> and the <a href="https://www.pubnub.com/blocks-catalog/initial-state-visualize-iot-data/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" data-href="https://www.pubnub.com/blocks-catalog/initial-state-visualize-iot-data/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Initial State BLOCK</a>. We will also be using <a href="https://www.pubnub.com/developers/realtime-data-streams/twitter-stream/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" data-href="https://www.pubnub.com/developers/realtime-data-streams/twitter-stream/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">PubNub’s live Twitter stream</a>.</p>
           <blockquote name="328f" id="328f" class="graf graf--blockquote graf-after--p">
            <em class="markup--em markup--blockquote-em">Note: PubNub’s Twitter stream only pulls in 50 messages a second (“only” ?) compared to the 6,000 that actually come in. I chose to use it instead of the Twitter API because I’m already throttling the number of messages I send to IBM Watson’s sentiment analysis to just 1,000/day to stay within their free trial guidelines (I was meeting this cap after about an hour of running the script unregulated). If you’re interested in sifting through all of the tweets every second because you have a less popular keyword, or if you’re paying for IBM’s services, checkout the last section of this post?—?“Part 7?—?The Unlimited Stream.</em>
           </blockquote>
           <h4 name="5bd7" id="5bd7" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--blockquote">Getting Started</h4>
           <p name="8761" id="8761" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">First things first, you need to create a PubNub account. <a href="https://www.pubnub.com/get-started/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" data-href="https://www.pubnub.com/get-started/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">You can register here</a>.</p>
           <p name="f608" id="f608" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Once you’re in and on the main page, scroll down to create an app. Apps are basically treated like projects, so each one has unique keys and blocks. Enter the name you want for your app (I named mine “Current Emotion in US”) and click “Create New App”. Click on your new app!</p>
           <figure name="22d9" id="22d9" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 592px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 84.5%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*sGOyn6NXanCFDlSCl1X9zQ.png" data-width="750" data-height="634" data-action="zoom" data-action-value="1*sGOyn6NXanCFDlSCl1X9zQ.png">

              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*sGOyn6NXanCFDlSCl1X9zQ.png">

             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="114d" id="114d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">You will be taken to the “Key Info” page for your app. We’ll need these keys later! Click on the Key box (should be named “Free”) to be taken to where you can enable features for said key set. Under the “Application add-ons” section, click on the slider next to “PubNub Blocks” to turn them on.</p>

           <h4 name="5ec8" id="5ec8" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--figure">Blocks</h4>
           <p name="7956" id="7956" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Click on the “Blocks” tab on the left hand side of the page. Here is where our Watson and Initial State code is going to go.</p>
           <p name="0033" id="0033" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Create a block and name it?—?I just called mine “Sentiment”. You should only have one key option because we didn’t create any extra. Click “Create”.</p>

           <h4 name="5ffe" id="5ffe" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--figure">IBM Watson Event&nbsp;Handler</h4>
           <p name="e771" id="e771" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Name this one “IBM Watson” and name the channel “sentiment-analysis”. Select “Before publish or fire” as the type.</p>

We are going to replace all of the code inside of the box with code for the <a href="https://www.pubnub.com/blocks-catalog/group-sentiment-analysis/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" data-href="https://www.pubnub.com/blocks-catalog/group-sentiment-analysis/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">IBM Watson: Sentiment and Context Analysis block</a>.</p>

           <p name="769b" id="769b" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Click the save icon to keep your changes. We’re going to add our Watson API key later.</p>
           <h4 name="f67c" id="f67c" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Initial State Event&nbsp;Handler</h4>
           <p name="fa45" id="fa45" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Click the “+” next to the IBM Watson tab. We can now create the Initial State event handler. I named it “Initial State” with the channel name “initial-state-streamer”. Select “After publish or fire” as the type.</p>

           <p name="7861" id="7861" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">Replace this handler’s code with the code for the <a href="https://www.pubnub.com/blocks-catalog/initial-state-visualize-iot-data/" data-href="https://www.pubnub.com/blocks-catalog/initial-state-visualize-iot-data/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Initial State block</a>. You can copy this code from the <a href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/InitialState.js" data-href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/InitialState.js" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">InitialState.js file</a>.</p>

         <div class="section-content">
          <div class="section-inner sectionLayout--insetColumn">
           <h3 name="eeb3" id="eeb3" class="graf graf--h3 graf--leading">Part 2?—?IBM Bluemix and IBM Watson&nbsp;Setup</h3>
           <figure name="d889" id="d889" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--h3">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 450px; max-height: 109px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 24.2%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*fRy97PTJNBjPJu3TEf3M-g.png" data-width="450" data-height="109">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*fRy97PTJNBjPJu3TEf3M-g.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*fRy97PTJNBjPJu3TEf3M-g.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*fRy97PTJNBjPJu3TEf3M-g.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="6073" id="6073" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">IBM Bluemix provides us access to the Watson APIs?—?most importantly, the sentiment analysis. You can use it for free for 30 days, too!</p>
           <h4 name="2126" id="2126" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Getting Started</h4>
           <p name="4810" id="4810" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">All good services start with a sign-up, so register at this link: <a href="https://console.ng.bluemix.net/registration/" data-href="https://console.ng.bluemix.net/registration/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">https://console.ng.bluemix.net/registration/</a></p>
           <p name="d40a" id="d40a" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">After a successful registration, you’ll have to confirm your account via email. Once back on the main page, navigate to <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">Products &amp; Services</em> -&gt; <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">Launch Bluemix</em>.</p>
           <p name="6d61" id="6d61" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">You’ll be prompted to name your “organization” and “space”?—?I just named mine “Twitter Stream” and “dev”.</p>
           <h4 name="db44" id="db44" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Get Your API&nbsp;Key</h4>
           <p name="0544" id="0544" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Next we need to provision the AlchemyAPI. Click on “Apps” or “Catalog” and either search for “AlchemyAPI” or look under <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">Services</em> -&gt; <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">Watson</em>.</p>
           <p name="82aa" id="82aa" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Clicking on the AlchemyAPI service will take you to a page describing it that also allows you to change the service and credentials names. If you scroll down you can see the pricing plans?—?“Free” should already be selected.</p>
           <p name="af27" id="af27" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Click “Create” to add the service!</p>
           <p name="bddc" id="bddc" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">You should be taking to a new service page. Click on the “Service Credentials” tab?—?you should see one set of credentials already created for you.</p>
           <p name="1f00" id="1f00" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Select the “View Credentials” drop-down to see your “apiKey”. Copy-paste this key to line 13 in your IBM Watson PubNub block.</p>
           <blockquote name="5aa3" id="5aa3" class="graf graf--blockquote graf-after--p">
            <em class="markup--em markup--blockquote-em">Note: IBM Bluemix just announced the </em>
            <a href="https://www.ibm.com/blogs/bluemix/2017/03/bye-bye-alchemyapi/" data-href="https://www.ibm.com/blogs/bluemix/2017/03/bye-bye-alchemyapi/" class="markup--anchor markup--blockquote-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><em class="markup--em markup--blockquote-em">retirement of the AlchemyAPI service</em></a>
            <em class="markup--em markup--blockquote-em">. They say to use instead the Natural Language Understanding service, also under Watson. This might change the IBM Sentiment Analysis block inside of PubNub?—?I’m sure they’ll update it soon!</em>
           </blockquote>
           <h4 name="f704" id="f704" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--blockquote">Test the&nbsp;Streamer</h4>
           <p name="92c6" id="92c6" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Go to the IBM Sentiment Analysis block inside of your PubNub app. Make sure that the block is Running and that you added your API key to the code.</p>
           <p name="d07b" id="d07b" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Copy-paste the following into the “Test Payload” box:</p>
           <pre name="0d3d" id="0d3d" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">{<br>    "session_id": 1,<br>    "text": "I am happy!"<br>}</code></pre>
           <p name="6971" id="6971" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Click “Publish”. If you see the following message in the debug console, then you successfully published to Watson and receive a sentiment score!</p>
           <figure name="2dbd" id="2dbd" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 47px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 6.7%;"></div>
             <img class="graf-image" data-image-id="1*rfmGTd4Jhio99H8i_WV9wQ.png" data-width="1470" data-height="98" data-action="zoom" data-action-value="1*rfmGTd4Jhio99H8i_WV9wQ.png" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*rfmGTd4Jhio99H8i_WV9wQ.png">
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="d929" id="d929" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure graf--trailing">Now to get our Initial State access key!</p>
          </div>

           <h3 name="8052" id="8052" class="graf graf--h3 graf--leading">Part 3— Initial&nbsp;State</h3>
           <figure name="af61" id="af61" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--h3">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 448px; max-height: 60px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 13.4%;"></div>
             <img class="graf-image" data-image-id="1*FlV4oT6bPO3eH3rS6DHJag.png" data-width="448" data-height="60" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*FlV4oT6bPO3eH3rS6DHJag.png">
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="2b10" id="2b10" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">We want to stream all of our sensor data to a cloud service and have that service turn our data into a nice interactive dashboard that updates in realtime. We are going to use <a href="https://www.initialstate.com/" data-href="https://www.initialstate.com/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Initial State</a>.</p>
           <h4 name="7d2a" id="7d2a" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Getting Started</h4>
           <p name="8c8a" id="8c8a" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Go to <a href="https://www.initialstate.com/app#/register/" data-href="https://www.initialstate.com/app#/register/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">https://www.initialstate.com/app#/register/</a> and create a new account.</p>
           <h4 name="9bb9" id="9bb9" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Get Your Access&nbsp;Key</h4>
           <p name="98c5" id="98c5" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Association with your Initial State account happens because of the Access Key parameter. If you go to your Initial State account in your web browser, click on your username in the top right, then go to “my account”, you will find your access key at the bottom of the page under “Streaming Access Keys”. It’s the long series of letters and numbers.</p>
           <figure name="63ca" id="63ca" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 334px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 47.699999999999996%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*2R2sRfg0-oXYI48xXvSsBQ.png" data-width="1280" data-height="610" data-action="zoom" data-action-value="1*2R2sRfg0-oXYI48xXvSsBQ.png">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*2R2sRfg0-oXYI48xXvSsBQ.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*2R2sRfg0-oXYI48xXvSsBQ.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*2R2sRfg0-oXYI48xXvSsBQ.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="d857" id="d857" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">Every time you create a data stream, that access key will direct that data stream to your account (so don’t share your key with anyone).</p>
           <p name="a64d" id="a64d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Copy-paste this key into line 27 of the Initial State block in PubNub.</p>
           <h4 name="ecab" id="ecab" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Test the&nbsp;Streamer</h4>
           <p name="706f" id="706f" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Go to the Initial State block inside of your PubNub app. Make sure that the block is Running and that you added your access key to the code.</p>
           <p name="e8a4" id="e8a4" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Copy-paste the following into the “Test Payload” box:</p>
           <pre name="b63b" id="b63b" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">{<br>     "events": [<br>         {<br>             "key": "temperature",<br>             "value": 16<br>         }<br>     ],<br>     "bucketKey": "pubnubTest"<br>}</code></pre>
           <p name="b94b" id="b94b" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Click “Publish”. If you see the following message in the debug console, then you successfully published to Initial State!</p>
           <figure name="552b" id="552b" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 22px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 3.1%;"></div>
             <img class="graf-image" data-image-id="1*p46XuGESb6AINJ9nP9maPA.png" data-width="1424" data-height="44" data-action="zoom" data-action-value="1*p46XuGESb6AINJ9nP9maPA.png" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*p46XuGESb6AINJ9nP9maPA.png">
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="7711" id="7711" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">Now let’s go check out our message in a dashboard.</p>
           <h4 name="6bf1" id="6bf1" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Profit</h4>
           <p name="dd7d" id="dd7d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Go back to your Initial State account in your web browser. We only sent our bucket key, so we need to manually create a bucket using the bucket shelf.</p>
           <figure name="5960" id="5960" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 570px; max-height: 418px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 73.3%;"></div>

               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*kDwCyeRajBWAgztVjqfxEg.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="5497" id="5497" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">At the top of your bucket shelf, click the +cloud icon to create a new streaming bucket. Name your bucket and check the “Configure Endpoint Keys” box to specify the bucket key.</p>
           <p name="4295" id="4295" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">This must match the key you just sent through PubNub so enter “pubnubTest”.</p>
           <p name="4bdb" id="4bdb" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Click the “Create” button at the bottom and the new bucket should be listed at the top of your shelf.</p>
           <figure name="266f" id="266f" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 386px; max-height: 388px;">

             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*UE091ERYD8rSfYfB7pqoug.png" data-width="386" data-height="388">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*UE091ERYD8rSfYfB7pqoug.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*UE091ERYD8rSfYfB7pqoug.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*UE091ERYD8rSfYfB7pqoug.png">

             </div>

           <p name="1d9d" id="1d9d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">Click on this bucket and you’ll see a tile that says “temperature” with a value of 16!</p>
           <p name="a8ca" id="a8ca" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p graf--trailing">Time to get everything working together.</p>

           <h3 name="3f77" id="3f77" class="graf graf--h3 graf--leading">Part 4— Putting it All&nbsp;Together</h3>
           <figure name="1467" id="1467" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--h3">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 614px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 87.7%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*d_i_gD52jeJi71ihWIt9rA.gif" data-width="860" data-height="754" data-action="zoom" data-action-value="1*d_i_gD52jeJi71ihWIt9rA.gif">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*d_i_gD52jeJi71ihWIt9rA.gif?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*d_i_gD52jeJi71ihWIt9rA.gif">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*d_i_gD52jeJi71ihWIt9rA.gif">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="cf41" id="cf41" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">Now that we’ve got the pieces working, it’s time to build our masterpiece.</p>
           <p name="2c30" id="2c30" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">We do want to check and make sure that consumption of <a href="https://www.pubnub.com/developers/realtime-data-streams/twitter-stream/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" data-href="https://www.pubnub.com/developers/realtime-data-streams/twitter-stream/?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">PubNub’s Twitter stream</a> is working, so let’s get to it!</p>
           <h3 name="b69e" id="b69e" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">Part 4a?—?Testing&nbsp;Twitter</h3>
           <figure name="a01f" id="a01f" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--h3">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 450px; max-height: 109px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 24.2%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*2bLe0DMfRZKP4hR-exvqlQ.png" data-width="450" data-height="109">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*2bLe0DMfRZKP4hR-exvqlQ.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*2bLe0DMfRZKP4hR-exvqlQ.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*2bLe0DMfRZKP4hR-exvqlQ.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="4204" id="4204" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">Twitter does have <a href="https://dev.twitter.com/rest/public" data-href="https://dev.twitter.com/rest/public" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">their own API</a>, but PubNub has made consuming it easy by providing us with a public subscription key. As I noted in Part 2, PubNub’s Twitter stream only pulls in 50 messages a second, but we’re throttling the number of messages sent to IBM Watson’s sentiment analysis to just 1,000/day anyways.</p>
           <p name="6e9d" id="6e9d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">If you’re interested in sifting through all of the tweets every second because you have a less popular keyword, or if you’re paying for IBM’s services, checkout the last section: <a href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/wiki/BONUS-Part-7.-The-Ultimate-Stream" data-href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/wiki/BONUS-Part-7.-The-Ultimate-Stream" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">BONUS?—?Part 7: The Ultimate Stream</a></p>
           <p name="68e3" id="68e3" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">I initially wrote this project in Python because that’s the language I’m most familiar in, but I’ve gone ahead and added Node JS versions of all the scripts too! These could easily be adapted into another language thanks to PubNub’s many SDKs.</p>
           <h4 name="ed1d" id="ed1d" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Python</h4>
           <p name="fbd3" id="fbd3" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">To use PubNub on your own machine (or perhaps a Raspberry Pi?), you need to install it using the command line:</p>
           <pre name="88ef" id="88ef" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">pip install 'pubnub&gt;=4.0.8'</code></pre>
           <p name="7ef0" id="7ef0" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">You can see other installation methods <a href="https://www.pubnub.com/docs/python/pubnub-python-sdk?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" data-href="https://www.pubnub.com/docs/python/pubnub-python-sdk?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">here</a>.</p>
           <blockquote name="4bf9" id="4bf9" class="graf graf--blockquote graf-after--p">
            <em class="markup--em markup--blockquote-em">Note: You may need to place “sudo” before the command if you receive a permissions error.</em>
           </blockquote>
           <p name="2933" id="2933" class="graf graf--p graf-after--blockquote">To see if the Twitter feed will work, just run the <a href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/twitterTest.py" data-href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/twitterTest.py" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">twitterTest.py</a> script! You can copy it to your computer by saving it to a folder you usually run code from or by creating a file with <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">nano twitterTest.py</code> and pasting it.</p>
           <p name="1ed7" id="1ed7" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Run the script:</p>
           <pre name="56e6" id="56e6" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">python twitterTest.py<br><br></code></pre>
           <p name="6e37" id="6e37" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Give it a second or two to actually find a tweet that matches our criteria on line 32 ([‘Trump’,’trump’,’POTUS’,’potus’]), and you should start seeing messages print out:</p>
           <pre name="d519" id="d519" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">@grassosteve @POTUS big time, which will lead to the other<br>Here we go Trump care conservative Republicans are not happy but from past told them to shut up and vote the way he tells them to so funny<br>#NativeNationsRise #yourlastterm @realDonaldTrump https://t.co/o2a4d7g3wT<br>45 says we should “invest in women’s health,” but has only nominated anti-choice #SCOTUS . #StopGorsuch #TrumpLies #TheResistance</code></pre>
           <p name="acc8" id="acc8" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">If that works, we can move on to the master script!</p>
           <h4 name="850b" id="850b" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Node</h4>
           <p name="c338" id="c338" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">To use PubNub on your own machine, you need to install it using the command line:</p>
           <pre name="9231" id="9231" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">npm install pubnub</code></pre>
           <p name="9063" id="9063" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">You can see other installation methods <a href="https://www.pubnub.com/docs/python/pubnub-python-sdk?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" data-href="https://www.pubnub.com/docs/python/pubnub-python-sdk?utm_source=Syndication&amp;utm_medium=Medium&amp;utm_campaign=SYN-CY17-Q2-Medium-April-17" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">here</a>.</p>
           <blockquote name="fc79" id="fc79" class="graf graf--blockquote graf-after--p">
            <em class="markup--em markup--blockquote-em">Note: You may need to place “sudo” before the command if you receive a permissions error.</em>
           </blockquote>
           <p name="cd6d" id="cd6d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--blockquote">To see if the Twitter feed will work, just run the <a href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/twitterTest.js" data-href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/twitterTest.js" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">twitterTest.js</a> script! You can copy it to your computer by saving it to a folder you usually run code from or by creating a file with <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">nano twitterTest.js</code> and pasting it.</p>
           <p name="ca91" id="ca91" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Run the script:</p>
           <pre name="071f" id="071f" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">node twitterTest.js</code></pre>
           <p name="e09a" id="e09a" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Give it a second or two to actually find a tweet that matches our criteria on line 16 (Trump, trump, or any capitalization of POTUS), and you should start seeing messages print out:</p>
           <pre name="79c5" id="79c5" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">@grassosteve @POTUS big time, which will lead to the other<br>Here we go Trump care conservative Republicans are not happy but from past told them to shut up and vote the way he tells them to so funny<br>#NativeNationsRise #yourlastterm @realDonaldTrump https://t.co/o2a4d7g3wT<br>45 says we should “invest in women’s health,” but has only nominated anti-choice #SCOTUS . #StopGorsuch #TrumpLies #TheResistance</code></pre>
           <p name="309e" id="309e" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">If that works, we can move on to the master script!</p>
           <h3 name="bcd7" id="bcd7" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">Part 4b?—?The&nbsp;Code</h3>
           <h4 name="0e73" id="0e73" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--h3">Python</h4>
           <p name="9b34" id="9b34" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">The final script is called <a href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/pubnubStream.py" data-href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/pubnubStream.py" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">pubnubStream.py</a>.</p>
           <p name="f4d1" id="f4d1" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">The most important thing you need to do before you try to run this script is add your PubNub keys:</p>
           <ul class="postList">
            <li name="23ae" id="23ae" class="graf graf--li graf-after--p">Lines 17 and 18: These keys can be found inside of the PubNub App you created in Part 1. Click on the “Key Info” tab and then on the “Free” key block to copy-paste them.</li>
           </ul>
           <h4 name="9d1b" id="9d1b" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--li">A Brief Overview of the Python&nbsp;Code</h4>
           <p name="d7c3" id="d7c3" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Lines 1–5 import all of our modules.</p>
           <p name="20bc" id="20bc" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Lines 7–20 are where we configure PubNub with both the public Twitter key and the private keys associated with our account.</p>
           <p name="2444" id="2444" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Lines 23–33 handle the results of any publish call and will tell us if a publish was successful.</p>
           <p name="1547" id="1547" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Lines 36–71 handle the subscription to the Twitter stream. If you want to change what keywords are looked for, you can do so on line 40 (‘Donald’ was omitted because I kept picking up tweets about McDonald’s). Starting at line 64, we actually handle the tweets?—?first searching for any of the keywords and then publishing the message to our sentiment-analysis channel (which is associated with the IBM Watson block).</p>
           <p name="b2a8" id="b2a8" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Lines 74–134 handle the subscription to the sentiment analysis output. On line 78 we specify our Initial State bucket key (“pubnubtrump”). We will need this to create our bucket in Initial State! Lines 99–134 handle the sentiment analysis response. We build the payload to send to our Initial State block here (using the merge function on lines 137–145) and then publish it.</p>
           <p name="ffcb" id="ffcb" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Lines 149–155 are where we configure our PubNub channel subscriptions and tell them which callback class to use.</p>
           <blockquote name="8c6a" id="8c6a" class="graf graf--blockquote graf-after--p">
            <em class="markup--em markup--blockquote-em">Note: On line 67 we are sleeping for 90 seconds before publishing to our sentiment analysis block. This line is present because the free tier for IBM Bluemix appears to cap users at 1,000 calls a day. Only sending every minute and a half ensures that we never reach that cap. If you want near-real-time action, just remove the sleep.</em>
           </blockquote>
           <h4 name="f16a" id="f16a" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--blockquote">Run the&nbsp;Script</h4>
           <p name="6306" id="6306" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Run the script with:</p>
           <pre name="d352" id="d352" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">python pubnubStream.py</code></pre>
           <p name="e8d4" id="e8d4" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">You should see the payload start printing out and output in your PubNub block debug console!</p>
           <h4 name="6c24" id="6c24" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Node</h4>
           <p name="4200" id="4200" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">The final script is called <a href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/pubnubStream.js" data-href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/pubnubStream.js" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">pubnubStream.js</a>.</p>
           <p name="c847" id="c847" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">The most important thing you need to do before you try to run this script is add your PubNub keys:</p>
           <ul class="postList">
            <li name="514d" id="514d" class="graf graf--li graf-after--p">Lines 10 and 11: These keys can be found inside of the PubNub App you created in Part 1. Click on the “Key Info” tab and then on the “Free” key block to copy-paste them.</li>
           </ul>
           <h4 name="9fd5" id="9fd5" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--li">A Brief Overview of the Node&nbsp;Code</h4>
           <p name="127b" id="127b" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Line 1 imports the PubNub modules.</p>
           <p name="97eb" id="97eb" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Lines 3–12 are where we configure PubNub with both the public Twitter key and the private keys associated with our account.</p>
           <p name="1f28" id="1f28" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Lines 17–40 handle the subscription to the Twitter stream. If you want to change what keywords are looked for, you can do so on line 25 (‘Donald’ was omitted because I kept picking up tweets about McDonald’s). Starting at line 25, we actually handle the tweets?—?first searching for any of the keywords and then publishing the message to our sentiment-analysis channel (which is associated with the IBM Watson block).</p>
           <p name="5198" id="5198" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Lines 42–88 handle the subscription to the sentiment analysis output. On line 48 we specify our Initial State bucket key (“pubnubtrump”). We will need this to create our bucket in Initial State! Lines 51–85 handle the sentiment analysis response. We build the payload to send to our Initial State block here and then publish it.</p>
           <p name="c17f" id="c17f" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Lines 91–99 are where we configure our PubNub channel subscriptions.</p>
           <blockquote name="7486" id="7486" class="graf graf--blockquote graf-after--p">
            <em class="markup--em markup--blockquote-em">Note: The free tier for IBM Bluemix appears to cap users at 1,000 calls a day. Running this script on the Trump and POTUS keywords hit that limit in 1–2 hours. You may want to implement some sort of delay or counter to keep from reaching the daily limit quickly.</em>
           </blockquote>
           <h4 name="2944" id="2944" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--blockquote">Run the&nbsp;Script</h4>
           <p name="6f2b" id="6f2b" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Run the script with</p>
           <pre name="1048" id="1048" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">node pubnubStream.js</code></pre>
           <p name="ec80" id="ec80" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">You should see the payload start printing out and output in your PubNub block debug console!</p>
           <p name="85ca" id="85ca" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Time to check the tweets out in a dashboard.</p>
           <h3 name="5501" id="5501" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">Part 5— Your Personal Dashboard</h3>
           <p name="800f" id="800f" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">Time to look at our dashboard! We need to create a bucket with the bucket key from our script like we did in Part 3.</p>
           <p name="0af8" id="0af8" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">So click the +cloud icon at the top of your bucket shelf to create a new streaming bucket. Name your bucket and check the “Configure Endpoint Keys” box to specify the bucket key.</p>
           <p name="593b" id="593b" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">This must match the key you just sent through PubNub so enter “pubnubtrump”. I named my bucket “Trump Twitter ?”.</p>
           <p name="264b" id="264b" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Click the “Create” button at the bottom and the new bucket should be listed at the top of your shelf.</p>
           <p name="04c1" id="04c1" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Click on that bucket and you should see Tiles pop up for Tweet, Positive Level, Neutral Level, Negative Level, and Score.</p>
           <figure name="5770" id="5770" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">

           <h3 name="1773" id="1773" class="graf graf--h3 graf--leading">Part 6— Add Tweet Locations</h3>
           <figure name="231e" id="231e" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--h3">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 158px;">

           <p name="273e" id="273e" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">Want to add maps to your dashboard that show which areas of the world are the most positive/negative/neutral?</p>
           <p name="8369" id="8369" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Just run the <a href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/pubnubStreamLocation.py" data-href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/pubnubStreamLocation.py" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">pubnubStreamLocation.py script</a> or the <a href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/pubnubStreamLocation.js" data-href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/pubnubStreamLocation.js" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">pubnubStreamLocation.js script</a> instead!</p>
           <p name="3ffe" id="3ffe" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p"><em class="markup--em markup--p-em">But first</em> you have to get a Google API key and install the geolocation module based on Google Maps.</p>
           <h4 name="306b" id="306b" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Get a Google API&nbsp;Key</h4>
           <p name="a0ab" id="a0ab" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">From the <a href="https://pypi.python.org/pypi/geolocation-python" data-href="https://pypi.python.org/pypi/geolocation-python" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">geolocation python page</a>:</p>
           <ol class="postList">
            <li name="9267" id="9267" class="graf graf--li graf-after--p">Visit the APIs console at <a href="https://code.google.com/apis/console" data-href="https://code.google.com/apis/console" class="markup--anchor markup--li-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">https://code.google.com/apis/console</a> and log in with your Google account</li>
            <li name="72e9" id="72e9" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li">Click the Services link from the left-hand menu and activate the Geocoding API service</li>
            <li name="131f" id="131f" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li">Your API key should now be available from the API Access page in the Simple API Access section</li>
           </ol>
           <p name="f6f1" id="f6f1" class="graf graf--p graf-after--li">Copy-paste this key into line 8.</p>
           <h4 name="dab8" id="dab8" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Install the Geocode&nbsp;Module</h4>
           <p name="d2cc" id="d2cc" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong"><em class="markup--em markup--p-em">Python?—?</em></strong>Install <a href="https://pypi.python.org/pypi/geolocation-python" data-href="https://pypi.python.org/pypi/geolocation-python" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">the geolocation module</a>:</p>
           <pre name="f5e3" id="f5e3" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">pip install geolocation-python</code></pre>
           <p name="4ce7" id="4ce7" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong"><em class="markup--em markup--p-em">Node?—?</em></strong>Install <a href="https://pypi.python.org/pypi/geolocation-python" data-href="https://pypi.python.org/pypi/geolocation-python" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">the geolocation module</a>:</p>
           <pre name="3db3" id="3db3" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">npm install @google/maps</code></pre>
           <blockquote name="8901" id="8901" class="graf graf--blockquote graf-after--pre">
            <em class="markup--em markup--blockquote-em">Note: If you receive a permissions error, add “sudo” to the front of the command</em>
           </blockquote>
           <h4 name="efe3" id="efe3" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--blockquote">For Node, edit the IBM Watson&nbsp;Block</h4>
           <p name="ac62" id="ac62" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">To get location data from Twitter and then stream it based on the associated tweet’s score, I just added 2 lines to the IBM Watson block inside of my PubNub app. You can copy that block code <a href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/IBMWatsonLocation.js" data-href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/IBMWatsonLocation.js" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">here</a>.</p>
           <p name="a658" id="a658" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p"><em class="markup--em markup--p-em">Be sure to put your IBM API key on line 13!</em></p>
           <h4 name="207c" id="207c" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Don’t Forget</h4>
           <p name="5961" id="5961" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Add your PubNub subscribe and publish keys to this script too!</p>
           <p name="4e6c" id="4e6c" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p graf--trailing">The <a href="http://support.initialstate.com/knowledgebase/articles/800232-tiles-data-view-type-map" data-href="http://support.initialstate.com/knowledgebase/articles/800232-tiles-data-view-type-map" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Map tiles</a> should automatically pop up inside of your Initial State bucket.</p>
          </div>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section name="ff79" class="section section--body">
         <div class="section-divider">
          <hr class="section-divider">
         </div>
         <div class="section-content">
          <div class="section-inner sectionLayout--insetColumn">
           <h3 name="24e0" id="24e0" class="graf graf--h3 graf--leading">Part 7— The Unlimited Stream&nbsp;(BONUS)</h3>
           <p name="713d" id="713d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">If you’re looking to sift through every single tweet that’s coming in you’ll need to consume the Twitter API directly. You can do this using the <a href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/pubnubStreamUnlimited.py" data-href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/pubnubStreamUnlimited.py" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">pubnubStreamUnlimited.py script</a> or the <a href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/pubnubStreamUnlimited.js" data-href="https://github.com/initialstate/pubnub-live-twitter-dashboard/blob/master/pubnubStreamUnlimited.js" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">pubnubStreamUnlimited.js script</a>.</p>
           <p name="5d7e" id="5d7e" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">If you’re planning on analyzing more than 1000 tweets a day, you’ll also have to upgrade your IBM Bluemix plan. The current AlchemyAPI plan looks like this:</p>
           <figure name="0756" id="0756" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 711px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 101.6%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*M-WKEE6u39Y-LNZ4ZokH-g.png" data-width="1132" data-height="1150" data-action="zoom" data-action-value="1*M-WKEE6u39Y-LNZ4ZokH-g.png">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*M-WKEE6u39Y-LNZ4ZokH-g.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*M-WKEE6u39Y-LNZ4ZokH-g.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*M-WKEE6u39Y-LNZ4ZokH-g.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="a48c" id="a48c" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">As I mentioned earlier, <a href="https://www.ibm.com/blogs/bluemix/2017/03/bye-bye-alchemyapi/" data-href="https://www.ibm.com/blogs/bluemix/2017/03/bye-bye-alchemyapi/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">IBM will soon be switching sentiment analysis over from the AlchemyAPI to Natural Language Understanding</a>. The pricing structure is slightly different:</p>
           <figure name="4505" id="4505" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 609px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 87%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*HatDDoqs6Nk49kLEgEoPEQ.png" data-width="984" data-height="856" data-action="zoom" data-action-value="1*HatDDoqs6Nk49kLEgEoPEQ.png">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*HatDDoqs6Nk49kLEgEoPEQ.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*HatDDoqs6Nk49kLEgEoPEQ.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*HatDDoqs6Nk49kLEgEoPEQ.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="fb09" id="fb09" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">Once you’ve figured out if you need to upgrade your IBM Bluemix service or not, you can get started using the Twitter API!</p>
           <h4 name="a785" id="a785" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Get Twitter API Credentials</h4>
           <p name="979c" id="979c" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">To get your Twitter API Credentials you will need to:</p>
           <ol class="postList">
            <li name="dbbc" id="dbbc" class="graf graf--li graf-after--p"><a href="https://dev.twitter.com/" data-href="https://dev.twitter.com/" class="markup--anchor markup--li-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Create a Twitter developer account</a></li>
            <li name="2ede" id="2ede" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li"><a href="https://apps.twitter.com/app/new" data-href="https://apps.twitter.com/app/new" class="markup--anchor markup--li-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Create an application</a></li>
            <li name="a3ca" id="a3ca" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li">Click on your app to be taken to its Details page. Click on the “Keys and Access Tokens” tab at the top to find and copy your Consumer Key, Consumer Secret, Access Token, and Access Token Secret (you may need to generate the access tokens).</li>
           </ol>
           <p name="d91b" id="d91b" class="graf graf--p graf-after--li">Copy-paste these keys into their respective spots on lines 11–14 in the Python script or lines 7–10 in the Node script.</p>
           <h4 name="ee0c" id="ee0c" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Install a Twitter&nbsp;Module</h4>
           <p name="620e" id="620e" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong"><em class="markup--em markup--p-em">Python?—?</em></strong><a href="http://tweepy.readthedocs.io/en/v3.5.0/index.html" data-href="http://tweepy.readthedocs.io/en/v3.5.0/index.html" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Tweepy</a> is an awesome library for accessing the Twitter API through Python. To install it run:</p>
           <pre name="d3d1" id="d3d1" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">pip install tweepy</code></pre>
           <p name="22cb" id="22cb" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong"><em class="markup--em markup--p-em">Node</em></strong>?—?You can install <a href="https://github.com/desmondmorris/node-twitter/" data-href="https://github.com/desmondmorris/node-twitter/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Twitter for Node.js</a> with:</p>
           <pre name="16f4" id="16f4" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">npm install twitter</code></pre>
           <blockquote name="ee30" id="ee30" class="graf graf--blockquote graf-after--pre">
            <em class="markup--em markup--blockquote-em">Note: If you receive a permissions error, add “sudo” to the front of the command</em>
           </blockquote>
           <h4 name="f24d" id="f24d" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--blockquote">Don’t Forget</h4>
           <p name="37cc" id="37cc" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Add your PubNub subscribe and publish keys to this script too!</p>
           <p name="0217" id="0217" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Now you should be all set to ingest the flood of data! I must say that I was super impressed watching PubNub successfully send messages to Watson, give me the response, and then send that data to Initial State even though I was absolutely hammering it. I mean, I hit my 1000 calls a day in less than 5 minutes!</p>
           <h3 name="2543" id="2543" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">Wrapping Up</h3>
           <p name="df80" id="df80" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3 graf--trailing">Boom! <a href="http://emojipedia.org/bomb/" data-href="http://emojipedia.org/bomb/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">?</a> You’ve done it! I’ve seen a ton of incredible and innovative realtime tutorials over my years, and this one is definitely one of my favorites! With PubNub BLOCKS and the vast number of partners, the sky’s the limit.</p>
          </div>
         </div>
